# Model Report: N5,8 (Per-Property)

> **ACAS Xu** вҖ” N5,8  
> Per-property experiments (property midpoint reference, no rule cap)  
> Generated 2026-03-20

**Model file:** `ACASXU_run2a_5_8_batch_2000.onnx`  
**Properties covered:** prop1, prop2, prop3, prop4 (4 total)  
**Experiment types:** full_rule, per_layer, impl_ablation

## How To Read Counts

- Each `Y/N/T/o` row is one verification query: `(property, Оө, true_class, target_label != true_class, rule)`.
- Self-target rows (`target_label == true_class`) are stored as `-` in the CSVs and are excluded from every denominator.
- Denominators in the summary tables count valid queries, not properties, models, or experiment directories.
- For the end-to-end pipeline and a worked example of counts such as `8/40`, see [`COUNTS_AND_PIPELINE.md`](COUNTS_AND_PIPELINE.md).


### What Is a Verification Query?

Each row in the tables below corresponds to a single call to the Marabou SMT solver.
A query is fully identified by the tuple **`(property, Оө, true_class, target_label, rule_type)`**.

**Concrete example вҖ” suppose we are looking at model N5,2, prop1, Оө = 0.05,
true\_class = 0, target\_label = 3, rule = ALWAYS\_OFF (Оұ = 0.9):**

**Step 1 вҖ” Choose the reference point.**
The reference point is the **midpoint** (element-wise center) of the VNNLIB
input box for the given property.  For prop1 of N5,2, this is a 5-dimensional
vector computed as `ref = (lower_bound + upper_bound) / 2` for each of the
5 ACAS Xu inputs.

**Step 2 вҖ” Build input constraints (LвҲһ ball).**
Marabou is told that the 5 network inputs must lie within:

```
ref[i] вҲ’ Оө  вүӨ  x[i]  вүӨ  ref[i] + Оө     for i = 0 вҖҰ 4
```

This defines a small hypercube ("Оө-ball") around the reference point.

**Step 3 вҖ” Add NAP constraints (the "rule" column).**
Depending on the rule type being tested:

| Rule type | What Marabou is told |
|-----------|---------------------|
| `none (baseline)` | No extra constraints вҖ” pure Marabou. |
| `ALWAYS_OFF` | For every neuron mined as "always off" for class 0 at Оұ вүҘ 0.9: force `pre_relu вүӨ 0` (neuron output = 0). |
| `ALWAYS_ON` | For every neuron mined as "always on" for class 0 at Оұ вүҘ 0.9: force `post_relu вүҘ 1e-6` (neuron fires). |
| `ALWAYS_ON+OFF` | Apply **both** ALWAYS_ON and ALWAYS_OFF constraints simultaneously. |
| `Impl LkвҶ’Lk+1` | For every implication rule mined between layers k and k+1 for class 0, add a disjunction constraint that encodes the implication (e.g., `AвҶ’B` becomes `(A is inactive) OR (B is active)`). |

These constraints tell the solver: "only search in the part of the Оө-ball
where the network's internal activation pattern matches what was observed
during sampling."  This prunes the search space dramatically.

**Step 4 вҖ” Add the adversarial output constraint.**
Marabou is told to look for an input where:

```
output[target_label]  вүҘ  output[true_class]
```

i.e., `output[3] вүҘ output[0]` in our example.  This asks: "can the network
be made to prefer action 3 over action 0 within the Оө-ball?"

**Step 5 вҖ” Solve and interpret the result.**

| Marabou answer | Meaning | Table symbol |
|----------------|---------|-------------|
| **UNSAT** | No such adversarial input exists вҖ” the network **cannot** be fooled into preferring target\_label over true\_class anywhere in the Оө-ball (given the NAP constraints). The property is **verified** for this query. | рҹҹў **Y** |
| **SAT** | An adversarial input **was found** вҖ” the network can be fooled. The property is **not verified**. | рҹ”ҙ **N** |
| **Timeout** | Marabou could not decide within 120 seconds. | рҹҹЎ **T/o** |

**Why do we test every (true\_class, target\_label) pair?**
The reference point's predicted class is its `true_class`.  We must check
that no *other* class can become dominant, so we test each of the other 4
classes as `target_label`.  This gives **4 queries per true\_class per Оө**.
If a property's input region contains samples predicted as multiple classes,
each predicted class becomes a separate `true_class`, multiplying the query
count accordingly (see the accounting table below).

**Per-model query accounting (the source of denominators such as `8/40`)**

| Property | True class(es) | Valid queries per Оө | Formula |
|----------|----------------|---------------------|---------|
| prop1 | 0, 2, 4 | 12 | 3 true classes Г— 4 non-self targets |
| prop2 | 0, 2, 4 | 12 | 3 true classes Г— 4 non-self targets |
| prop3 | 2 | 4 | 1 true classes Г— 4 non-self targets |
| prop4 | 2 | 4 | 1 true classes Г— 4 non-self targets |
| **Total** | вҖ“ | **32** | **12 + 12 + 4 + 4** |

<!-- denominator-explanation -->

**Why the denominator is 32:**  
This model has 4 properties. For each property, we count how many distinct classes the network predicts within that property's input region (from sampling), then multiply by 4 (the 4 other target labels, excluding the self-target). Summing across properties:

- prop1 has 3 true class(es) (0, 2, 4) вҶ’ 3 Г— 4 = 12 queries
- prop2 has 3 true class(es) (0, 2, 4) вҶ’ 3 Г— 4 = 12 queries
- prop3 has 1 true class(es) (2) вҶ’ 1 Г— 4 = 4 queries
- prop4 has 1 true class(es) (2) вҶ’ 1 Г— 4 = 4 queries

**Total per Оө = 12 + 12 + 4 + 4 = 32.**  
So every `вҖҰ/32` you see in the tables below means "out of 32 valid verification queries at that epsilon."  
The `Total Y%` column divides by 32 Г— 4 = **128** (summed across all four Оө values).
